## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material, which is a core problem in constitutive modeling. Stress typically increases with strain (elastic/plastic hardening) and decreases with increasing temperature (thermal softening).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic regime)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = c0 * (1 - c1 * T) * epsilon (linear elasticity with thermal softening)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Hollomon-type plastic hardening)
- Johnson-Cook strain-temperature form: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 - c2 * T**c3) (combined hardening and thermal softening)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon) (saturating stress-strain curve)
- Voce with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon)) * (1 - c3 * T**c4) (saturating hardening with temperature effect)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse form: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic + plastic combined)
- Thermally-activated flow stress: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (Arrhenius-type thermal activation)
- Ludwik model: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Ludwik with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(c3 * T) (yield + hardening with thermal activation)
- Swift hardening: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (shifted power law for pre-strained materials)
- Polynomial thermal modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (quadratic temperature-dependent stiffness)
- Hyperbolic sine flow: sigma = c0 * T * arcsinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 * T)) (Garofalo/Sellars-Tegart type creep model)
- Linear thermal + power hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 - T) (linear thermal softening with power hardening)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening → multiplicative factor (1 - c*T**n) or (Tm - T)**n representing distance from melting point
- Strain hardening saturation → exponential approach to limit: c0*(1 - exp(-c1*epsilon)), indicating dislocation density saturation
- Elastic-plastic transition → additive decomposition: linear term (c0*epsilon) + nonlinear term (c1*epsilon**c2)
- Temperature-dependent yield stress → yield term that decreases with T: c0*exp(c1*T) or c0*(1 - c1*T)
- Creep/thermally-activated deformation → sinh or arcsinh functions of strain scaled by Boltzmann-type temperature factor
- Separable strain-temperature coupling → product form f(epsilon)*g(T), indicating independent hardening and softening mechanisms
- Non-separable coupling → epsilon*T cross terms or T-dependent hardening exponent, indicating mechanism changes with temperature
- Strain offset for initial yield → (epsilon + c0)**c1 rather than epsilon**c1, representing pre-existing dislocation density
